Huygens Professional software . 3 Methods 3 . 1 Preparation of Polyacrylamide Matrices ( Adapted from [ 25 ] ) 1 . Clean 22 (cid:1) 22 mm coverslips are stored in 70 % ethanol . 2 . Dry the coverslips by ﬂaming to remove the ethanol . 3 . Place the desired number of coverslips ( after removing ethanol ) in freshly prepared KOH solution ( see Note 1 ) . 4 . Sonicate the solution using a probe sonicator and the following program ( we use a Sonics VibraCell Model No . VCX130 ) , Time—20 min , Pulse—4 s ON , 3 s OFF , Amplitude—50 % . 5 . Post sonication , discard KOH solution with care . Wash cover - slips with Milli - Q water . Repeat this steps 4 and 5 times . Post washes , store coverslips in Milli - Q . 6 . Prepare fresh APTES solution in a Falcon tube . Dispense 1 mL in each well of a 6 - well plate . Cover the plate with lid . 7 . Lift a single coverslip using ﬁne forceps and dip it into 100 % methanol ( around 15 – 20 mL in a Falcon tube ) to remove traces of water and then place it in a well of the 6 - well plate Imaging the Effect of Matrix Stiffness on the Genome 185 containing the APTES silanizing solution . Repeat this step with the remaining coverslips . 8 . Place the 6 - well plate ( s ) for 30 – 45 min on a shaker with very slow uniform shaking . 9 . After the silane treatment , wash the coverslips with Milli - Q water 3 – 4 times in the 6 - well plate itself . 10 . In a 15 cm petri dish with lid , spread a soft tissue paper . Carefully place the washed coverslips in the dish , with treated side facing up . Close the lid and place in a hybridization oven set to 50 (cid:4) C for 30 – 45 min for drying the coverslips . 11 . After the coverslips are completely dry , place them back in the 6 - well plates and add freshly prepared ~ 1 . 5 mL of 0 . 5 % Glutar - aldehyde solution ( in 1 (cid:1) PBS ) to each well . Place the plate ( s ) on a shaker with fast shaking ( such that the coverslips stay immersed in the solution and air bubbles are not formed ) for 30 min . 12 . Wash the coverslips with Milli - Q water 3 – 4 times . Post - wash , place the coverslips face up in the 15 cm dish containing soft tissue and allow the coverslips to completely dry . 13 . Polyacrylamide matrices of well - deﬁned compliances can be generated by mixing acrylamide and bisacrylamide solutions in speciﬁc concentrations . For matrices of ~ 2 kPa and ~ 55 kPa , prepare acrylamide – bisacrylamide solution as follows : ~ 2 kPa polyacrylamide matrices : 5 % acrylamide and 0 . 2 % bisacrylamide . ~ 55 kPa polyacrylamide matrices : 12 % acrylamide and 0 . 6 % bisacrylamide . 14 . First , prepare acrylamide – bisacrylamide solution in Milli - Q water without APS and TEMED . Then , arrange glass slides in 15 cm dishes—three slides ﬁt in one dish . Each slide can be used to prepare polyacrylamide matrices on two coverslips . Next , polish each slide with ~ 50 μ L Sigmacote solution to make them hydrophobic . 15 . Add APS and TEMED to the acrylamide – bisacrylamide solu - tion and mix it gently . Dispense 35 μ L on one end of the glass slide . Similarly , dispense another 35 μ L on the other end of the glass slide . 16 . Gently invert a completely dry coverslip over the drop ensuring that air bubbles are not introduced , leaving a small edge of the coverslip hanging over the edge of the slide . Repeat this proce - dure for the remaining coverslips . 17 . These matrices ( prepared by the “sandwich method” ) take ~ 10 min to completely polymerize . Once polymerization of the gel is evident , submerge the slides in a petri dish containing 186 Roopali Pradhan and Kundan Sengupta 50 mM HEPES solution . The coverslips are removed by apply - ing gentle pressure to the overhanging edge of the coverslip with forceps—the coverslip ( with PAA matrix ) will be dis - lodged from the slide . Gently lift the coverslip and place it in a 6 - well plate containing 50 mM HEPES buffer—gel side facing up ( see Note 2 ) . 18 . These coverslips with the polyacrylamide matrices can be stored at 4 (cid:4) C for 2 weeks in 50 mM HEPES buffer . 3 . 2 Activation of Polyacrylamide Matrices 1 . Thaw a 40 μ L Sulfo - SANPAH aliquot and prepare a working solution by diluting it up to 1 mL with Milli - Q water . 2 . Place the coverslip with the PAA matrices—gel side facing up , on a Paraﬁlm laid out in a 15 cm petri dish , inside tissue culture laminar - ﬂow cabinet . Add ~ 150 μ L of Sulfo - SANPAH working solution on the matrix . Repeat this for all the coverslips , making sure that the gel does not dry . 3 . Place the petri dish at ~ 10 cm from the UV source ( 300 – 350 nm ) and perform 2 UV cycles of ~ 20 min each . 4 . After the UV cycles , place the polyacrylamide matrices in 6 - well plate containing 1 . 5 mL DPBS ( gel side facing up ) . Wash the coverslips 2 – 3 times with DPBS to remove excess Sulfo - SANPAH . To each polyacrylamide gel , add ~ 1 . 5 mL Collagen I solution ( 100 μ g / mL in DPBS ) . Store the coverslips at either 4 (cid:4) C for later use or at 37 (cid:4) C for 3 h for immediate use . 5 . Clean and sterile glass coverslips ( without PAA matrix ) are also kept for coating with Collagen I solution ( 100 μ g / mL in DPBS ) at 4 (cid:4) C ( or 37 (cid:4) C ) to be used as controls ( see Note 3 ) . 3 . 3 Plating Cells on Polyacrylamide Matrices and Fixation for 3D - FISH 1 . Wash 70 – 80 % conﬂuent cells growing on tissue culture plastic with 2 – 3 mL DPBS twice . 2 . Add 0 . 05 % trypsin – EDTA solution and incubate the cells at 37 (cid:4) C for 3 – 4 min . As the cells detach from the culture dish , neutralize the trypsin with culture medium – either RPMI 1640 or DMEM . 3 . Centrifuge the cell suspension at 110 g , 10 (cid:4) C for 5 min . 4 . Remove the coverslips—with and without polyacrylamide matrices , from 4 (cid:4) C and discard the Collagen I solution . Wash the coverslips with ~ 1 . 5 mL DPBS thrice by gentle swir - ling . Add culture medium ( RPMI 1640 or DMEM , 2 mL in a single well of a 6 - well plate ) and incubate at 37 (cid:4) C until cells are ready for plating . 5 . After centrifugation , discard the supernatant and resuspend the cell pellet in 1 mL culture medium . Count and seed ~ 0 . 5 (cid:1) 10 6 cells per coverslip for ~ 2 kPa , ~ 55 kPa polyacrylamide matrices and glass coverslips ( without any PAA matrix ) . Imaging the Effect of Matrix Stiffness on the Genome 187 6 . Incubate cells in 37 (cid:4) C / 5 % CO 2 incubator , in contact with extracellular matrices of different stiffness properties for the desired duration . 7 . Take the cells out of the incubator and gently wash with 1 (cid:1) PBS twice for 5 min ( see Note 4 ) . 8 . Following the second PBS wash , add fresh 1 (cid:1) PBS to the cells and place on ice for 4 – 5 min . 9 . Discard PBS , and incubate cells with 1 mL CSK buffer for 5 – 7 min ( cell type speciﬁc ) in order to digest the cytoskeleton . This step is carried out on ice . 10 . After 5 – 7 min ( cell type speciﬁc ) , remove CSK and immediately add 4 % Paraformaldehyde solution to the cells for ﬁxation for 12 – 14 min . 11 . CSK mediated cytoskeletal digestion must be monitored under a brightﬁeld microscope , until ( 1 ) the nucleus appears darker than its surroundings ( i . e . , enhanced contrast ) and ( 2 ) only a few cells lift off the coverslip , suggestive of optimal digestion . Suboptimal CSK treatment compromises hybridization of ﬂuo - rescent probes or chromosome paints . While prolonged CSK treatment leads to considerable loss of cells . 12 . Following ﬁxation with PFA , gently wash cells with 0 . 1 M Tris – HCl solution ( pH 7 . 4 ) for 7 min , and thrice with 1 (cid:1) PBS for 5 min each . 13 . Permeabilize cells with 0 . 5 % Triton X - 100 solution for 15 min . 14 . Discard the Triton X - 100 solution and immediately add 20 % Glycerol solution . Incubate cells for 45 – 60 min at RT . 15 . Subject cells to freeze - thaw cycles using liquid nitrogen . Dis - pense liquid nitrogen in an open styrofoam container . Using a pair of ﬁne forceps , gently lift the coverslip and brieﬂy dip it in liquid nitrogen . Remove the coverslip and place it face up on a soft tissue for it to thaw , without allowing it to dry . As soon as the coverslip thaws , place it back in the glycerol solution . This step is carried out for each coverslip 5 – 7 times [ CAUTION : PAA matrices crack upon excessive liquid nitrogen treatment . The matrices should be carefully monitored for cracks during freeze - thaw cycles . Terminate freeze – thaw cycles if matrices crack . Importantly , nuclei on polyacrylamide matrices and glass coverslips are typically subject to an equal number of freeze – thaw cycles ] . 16 . Wash the nuclei with 1 (cid:1) PBS , thrice for 5 min each . 17 . Incubate in 0 . 1 N HCl for 10 min at RT . 18 . Wash the coverslips with 1 (cid:1) PBS , thrice for 5 min each . After the ﬁnal wash , add 2 mL of 50 % Formamide / 2 (cid:1) SSC to the coverslips . These can be stored in 50 % Formamide / 2 (cid:1) SSC at 4 (cid:4) C till further use ( preferably use within 1 – 2 weeks ) . 188 Roopali Pradhan and Kundan Sengupta 3 . 4 Probe Preparation and 3D - FISH 1 . Puriﬁed BAC DNA ( RP11 - 702H12 for LAMTOR2 and RP11 - 805D24 for CRABP2 ) is used for generating ﬂuores - cently labeled probes . Labeling reaction is carried out following instructions for the Nick Translation Mix , at 15 (cid:4) C for 3 h and terminated using 0 . 5 M EDTA solution ( pH 8 . 0 ) at 65 (cid:4) C for 10 min . Nick translated DNA is precipitated using Salmon sperm DNA , ethanol and 3 M Sodium Acetate , while Human Cot I DNA ( 1 μ g per reaction ) is added to decrease back - ground due to cross - hybridization of repeat rich sequences . Fluorescently labelled probes are re - suspended in deionized formamide and Master Mix containing dextran sulfate and 2 (cid:1) SSC . 2 . Take required volumes of chromosome paints or ﬂuorescently labeled BAC DNA probes ( 6 – 7 μ L ) is sufﬁcient for a 22 (cid:1) 22 mm coverslip ) and equilibrate at 37 (cid:4) C and 750 rpm ( 60 g ) for 7 min in a thermomixer , followed by denaturation at 80 (cid:4) C for 6 min and quick chill on ice for 2 – 3 min . Preanneal - ing is carried out at 37 (cid:4) C for 60 min without shaking . 3 . Thaw coverslips at RT . After preannealing the probe , spot ~ 6 – 7 μ L of chromosome paint or ﬂuorescently labeled BAC DNA probe onto a clean slide and invert the coverslip ( with the ﬁxed nuclei facing down ) on it , taking care that no bubbles are introduced . 4 . Seal the coverslip using nail polish and co - denature the ﬁxed nuclei with the chromosome paint / probe at 80 (cid:4) C for ( 1 ) 10 min—nuclei on glass coverslips , ( 2 ) 12 min—nuclei on 2 kPa matrices and ( 3 ) 15 min—nuclei on 55 kPa matrices . [ NOTE : These time points are only indicative and need to be optimized for each cell and matrix type independently . ] 5 . Place slides in a humid hybridization chamber , prepared by placing moist paper towels soaked in 50 % Formamide / 2 (cid:1) SSC inside an air - tight container and store at 37 (cid:4) C for 48 h . 6 . After hybridization , carefully remove nail polish , and place the coverslips in a 6 - well plate ( gel side facing up ) containing ~ 2 mL 2 (cid:1) SSC buffer per well . 7 . Rinse coverslips thrice for 5 min each in 50 % Formamide / 2 (cid:1) SSC ( prewarmed at 45 (cid:4) C for at least 45 min before use ) . 8 . Rinse coverslips thrice for 5 min each in 0 . 1 (cid:1) SSC ( prewarmed at 60 (cid:4) C for at least 45 min before use ) . 9 . Incubate coverslips in 0 . 1 % Tween 20 / 4 (cid:1) SSC at RT for 30 – 45 s , followed by counterstaining using 0 . 05 μ g / mL DAPI solution for ~ 2 – 2 . 5 min . 10 . Rinse coverslips once with 2 (cid:1) SSC for 5 min . Imaging the Effect of Matrix Stiffness on the Genome 189 11 . Mounting coverslips—Spot 5 – 6 μ L Antifade on a clean glass slide and invert the coverslip ( gel side facing down ) on it taking care that no bubbles are introduced . The excess Antifade is wiped off using soft tissue and the coverslip sealed with nail polish ( see Notes 5 and 6 ) . 3 . 5 Imaging and Analyses Confocal imaging is performed as described in Subheading 2 . 4 , and images are analyzed as follows : Radial distance measurements of chromosome territories —3D reconstructions and distance measurements are performed using Image - Pro Plus software ( v 7 . 1 ) . Brieﬂy , LSM ﬁles with optical sections ( z ¼ 0 . 34 μ m ) of hybridized nuclei are subjected to 3D surface rendering . Individual nuclei are cropped for 3D reconstruc - tion . The acquired images are thresholded for each of the red , green , and blue channels . The geometric center of the DAPI - stained nucleus ( blue channel ) and the chromosome territories ( red and green channels ) are determined using Image - Pro Plus software , and the distance between the center of the nucleus and that of the territory is measured ( A ) . The vector A from the center of nucleus ( N ) to that of the chromosome territory ( C ) is extended to a third collinear point on the nuclear periphery ( R ) . The distance ( B ) between the center of the nucleus and point R is calculated . The relative distance of a chromosome territory from the center of the nucleus is expressed as a percentage of its total distance from the center of the nucleus to the nuclear periphery , % Radial Dis - tance ¼ ( A / A + B ) (cid:1) 100 ( Fig . 1 ) [ 13 ] . Measurement of shortest distance from DAPI edge —Distances of gene loci from the nuclear periphery ( in μ m ) in 3D using the DAPI staining to demarcate the edge of the nucleus . Brieﬂy , surface rendering is performed for the gene loci ( red and green channel ) and the nucleus ( DAPI signal—blue channel ) using Huygens Pro - fessional software . The surface rendered DAPI signal is used as an envelope anchor , Centre of Mass ( CM ) is determined for each gene locus and closest distance between the CM and surface of anchor is measured . Figures 2 , 3 , 4 , and 5 show 3D - FISH hybridization for CT18 and 19 in DLD - 1 , HCT116 , U2OS and HT1080 cells . Figure 6 shows 3D - FISH hybridization for LAMTOR2 and CRABP2 . Both genes are present on Chr . 1 and upregulated in DLD - 1 cells exposed to softer 2 kPa matrices for 90 min— LAMTOR2 ( 1q22 , ~ nine fold up ) and CRABP2 ( 1q23 . 2 , ~ three fold up ) . 4 Notes 1 . Coverslips may crack anytime during the entire procedure . It is therefore advisable to have backup coverslips prepared . 190 Roopali Pradhan and Kundan Sengupta 2 . If the treatment of the coverslips is non - uniform ( e . g . , the coverslips are not fully immersed in all the solutions ) , the polyacrylamide matrix will not completely adhere to the cover - slips . Such a matrix , detached from any region of the coverslip , should not be used for further experiments . 3 . If cells do not adhere to the collagen - coated polyacrylamide matrices , either the activation of Sulfo - SANPAH or the colla - gen coating is suboptimal . ( 1 ) Activation of Sulfo - SANPAH — Upon UV treatment , the color of Sulfo - SANPAH darkens ( light orange to dark orange ) , which is indicative of successful UV treatment . ( 2 ) Collagen coating —In our hands , collagen coating is uniform and optimal when performed at 4 (cid:4) C for at least 24 h prior to cell plating . 4 . Each cell type spreads to varying extents on PAA matrices of different stiffness properties . This duration needs to be care - fully optimized for each cell type before performing FISH . 5 . If chromosome territory or gene loci hybridization is unsuc - cessful , either CSK treatment or nuclear permeabilization is suboptimal . ( 1 ) CSK treatment —As mentioned previously , CSK digestion is a crucial step and should be optimized for every cell line . ( 2 ) Cell and nuclear permeabilization —Permea - bilization using 0 . 5 % Triton X - 100 can be prolonged up to 20 min . Nat Protoc 7 : 2056 – 2066 Imaging the Effect of Matrix Stiffness on the Genome 197 Chapter 13 Targeted Manipulation / Repositioning of Subcellular Structures and Molecules Kathrin S . Heinz and M . Cristina Cardoso Abstract Technical advances in live - cell imaging have made cell biology into a highly dynamic ﬁeld , allowing the visualization and quantiﬁcation of complex processes in individual cells and in real time . To follow changes and to speciﬁcally manipulate factors potentially involved in processes like DNA replication , transcription or repair , we set up a universal targeting approach , allowing directed manipulation of subcellular structures and molecules therein . This strategy is based on the very strong and speciﬁc interaction of GFP and GFP - binding nanobody . We describe in detail how to set up the targeting approach with appropriate controls , as well as how to improve and validate its efﬁciency and ﬁnally provide exemplary applications . Key words Green ﬂuorescent protein , GFP - binding nanobody , Live - cell microscopy , Protein – protein interaction , Targeted manipulation , Targeted repositioning 1 Introduction The visualization and quantiﬁcation of processes in individual cells and in real time enables the tracking of spatiotemporal changes and evaluating their potential impact and function . To answer funda - mental questions and understand the function of individual factors on multiplex processes it is important to be able to study the role of any factor X on any process Y . Thus , it is of major advantage to speciﬁcally manipulate DNA , RNA , proteins , or even subcellular structures in a controlled and targeted manner . The manipulation of proteins localization via bait and prey type of approaches , such as ﬂuorescence two - hybrid / tri - hybrid assays [ 1 , 2 ] among others , is a very useful tool to study protein – protein interactions . It would be of major advantage to use the same principles to manipulate the localization of entire subcellular structures and study complex questions like the effect of location on function . Here , we describe a strategy that is based on the strong and highly speciﬁc interaction of GFP and GFP - binding protein ( GBP ) . GBP is a recombinant 13 - kDa GFP binding fragment derived from Yaron Shav - Tal ( ed . ) , Imaging Gene Expression : Methods and Protocols , Methods in Molecular Biology , vol . 2038 , https : / / doi . org / 10 . 1007 / 978 - 1 - 4939 - 9674 - 2 _ 13 , © Springer Science + Business Media , LLC , part of Springer Nature 2019 199 a llama single chain V H H antibody [ 3 , 4 ] ( Fig . 1 ) . Because of the high afﬁnity of GFP and GBP with a K d in the subnanomolar range , it is possible to target any desired factor and even reposition large genomic regions when both factors are coexpressed in cells . The efﬁciency and strength of this targeting approach becomes obvious , since it is possible to even reposition constitutive heterochromatin in murine cells to the nuclear periphery to study the effect of nuclear position on basic cellular processes such as DNA replication and epigenetic composition [ 5 ] . In this chapter , we explain in detail how to design an individual and successful targeting assay and how to develop the appropriate controls . Depending on the question to be addressed , different control setups are possible ( Fig . 2a ) . A control setup with no targeting or manipulation is achieved by transfection of X - GFP alone without the additional transfection of the GBP - carrying counterpart ( Fig . 2a setup 1 ) . To rule out any effect caused by the overexpression of factor Y one could remove the GBP part and simply transfect factor Y with X - GFP , leading to no interaction ( Fig . 2a setup 2 ) . Furthermore , the disruption of the targeting for a control setup can be achieved by replacing GFP by RFP , which does not interact with GBP ( Fig . 2a setup 3 ) . Lastly , it is possible to cotransfect X - GFP with a GBP—carrying an inactive form of pro - tein Y ( Fig . 2a setup 4 ) . In the case of enzymes one could inactivate the catalytic activity by site - directed mutagenesis and thus target an D ES I G N CMV GBP Y CMV X GFP TARGETING APPROACH A B DNA replication . . . Fig . 1 ( a ) Schematic representation of the targeted manipulation approach . The strategy is based on the strong interaction of GFP and GFP binding protein ( GBP ) . Both counterparts can be designed and cloned to any desired factor X and Y to target DNA , RNA , or even subcellular structures . Upon coexpression of both constructs , the interaction of GFP with GBP is strong enough to even reposition large genomic regions . ( b ) The application range of the targeting approach is broad and potential processes include DNA replication , epigenetics , DNA repair , and DNA transcription . Targeting of structures to reposition them is one application but also targeting of factors to a desired locus . Successful targeting can be achieved in different cell lines , depending on the factors used and processes under study 200 Kathrin S . Heinz and M . Cristina Cardoso inactive version of the factor to the desired location . Furthermore , we present in detail how the validation of the targeting and control setup is accomplished ( Fig . 2b ) . Different parameters need to be considered when optimizing the targeting approach , from the best ratio of both plasmid constructs during transfection to incubation time after transfection up to validation of transfection efﬁciency . Optimization of ratio of plasmids ( 1 : 1 - 3 : 3 ) Incubation time Transfection CMV GBP Y CMV X GFP low mid high % % % Targeting level Fig . 2 Schematic representation of the design of appropriate controls and the validation thereof . ( a ) The design of appropriate controls is ﬂexible and dependent on the question to be answered . Here , we show different strategies to disrupt targeting , leading to a control setup . First , an untargeted state is achieved by transfecting only the X - GFP part without any interaction partner ( setup 1 ) . Furthermore , the X - GFP is transfected with Y alone , without the GBP part , which is required for interaction of both constructs . One advantage of this method is to elucidate , whether the overexpression of Y alone already leads to an effect on the investigated process ( setup 2 ) . Another strategy to achieve an untargeted control state , especially when targeting a factor to a desired locus , is the inactivation of factor Y . If Y is an enzyme , one could inactivate the catalytic activity by point mutation ( setup 4 ) . As GBP interacts with GFP but not with RFP , another strategy includes the design of an RFP - tagged X , which no longer interacts with the GBP - Y counterpart ( setup 3 ) . ( b ) After successful design of controls , the validation thereof as well as of the targeting is of upmost importance . The ﬁrst step is to transfect cells with the appropriate constructs and validate the perfect ratio of plasmids to achieve a targeting signal . The incubation time after transfection needs also to be optimized . When cells show a targeted signal , the transfection efﬁciency can be determined , meaning the percentage of cells expressing the constructs and showing the desired targeted signal . The power of targeting could be categorized into different levels ( e . g . , low , mid , and high targeting ) to check which level is the most desired one and depicts no toxic effects . Control and targeted cells should show their characteristic morphology to rule out toxic effects , which can lead to cell death Targeted Manipulation 201 B INACTIVE FACTOR ACTIVE FACTOR CMV GBP Y * CMV macroH2a GFP for Xi CMV HP1 beta GFP for Xa or CMV GBP Y CMV macroH2a GFP for Xi CMV HP1 beta GFP for Xa or T AR G E T I N G O F F AC T O R S M i c r o t u s ca b r e r ae Xa Xi TARGETING CMV MeCP2 GFP CMV LaminB1 GBP CHR O M O C E N T E R R EP O S I T I O N I N G CONTROL CMV MeCP2 GFP CMV LaminB1 A Fig . 3 Application of the targeting approach to constitutive and facultative in different cell lines and species . ( a ) Repositioning of constitutive heterochromatin in various cell lines . MeCP2 - GFP was coexpressed with LaminB1 without the GBP . No interaction of both targeting parts took place and thus constitutive heterochro - matin was distributed throughout the whole nucleus . Upon coexpression of MeCP2 - GFP and GBP - LaminB1 , constitutive heterochromatin was repositioned to the nuclear lamina , resulting in a clear peripheral targeting ring . The targeting strategy was performed in different somatic and embryonic mouse cell lines : MEF , C2C12 , and J1 . ( b ) Macro - H2a and HP1 - beta were tagged to GFP to either recognize the heterochromatin of the inactive X chromosome ( Xi ) or the active X chromosome ( Xa ) in Microtus cabrerae female ﬁbroblasts . Upon coexpression with GBP - Y , where Y is any desired factor , Y is transported to the Xi or Xa . For the control setup , factor Y could be inactivated by , for example , point mutation 202 Kathrin S . Heinz and M . Cristina Cardoso This targeting strategy was successfully used to study the effect of nuclear position of DNA on its DNA replication timing . For this study constitutive heterochromatin was repositioned to the nuclear periphery into an environment of mid - replicating facultative het - erochromatin [ 6 ] . MeCP2 as a methyl - cytosine binding protein [ 7 ] was used as X and tagged to GFP . MeCP2 binds methylated cyto - sines , which are highly abundant in constitutive heterochromatin . The latter forms micrometer sized aggregates in mouse cells termed chromocenters [ 8 ] . LaminB1 , as a component of the nuclear lamina , was used as Y and was transfected without the GBP - counterpart to give normally localized GFP - labeled chromo - centers ( Fig . 3a ) . To reposition constitutive heterochromatin , MeCP2 - GFP and GBP - LaminB1 were coexpressed , leading to a clear green targeting ring at the nuclear periphery . With this approach constitutive heterochromatin was recognized , labeled , and repositioned in different cells , including mouse embryonic ﬁbroblasts ( MEF [ 9 ] ) , embryonic stem cells ( J1 [ 10 ] ) , and myo - blasts ( C2C12 [ 11 ] ) . Additionally , we were able to transport spe - ciﬁc factors to a desired location . We transported factor Y ( a histone acetylating enzyme ) to the heterochromatin of the inactive X chro - mosome ( Xi ) with the help of the macroH2a histone variant [ 12 ] and to the active X chromosome ( Xa ) with the help of HP1 beta [ 13 , 14 ] in Microtus cabrerae [ 15 ] cells ( Fig . 3b ) . For this purpose , an additional control should be added including the inactive form of the enzyme . All in all , this experimental strategy enables speciﬁc tethering of any DNA , RNA , protein , or even subcellular structures of interest to any desired location and lays the ground for controlled manipu - lation of factors such as epigenetic regulators , transcription factors , or ultimately subcellular localization of structures . 2 Materials All materials and solutions used for cell culture , ﬁxed cell studies , and live - cell microscopy must be sterile . 1 . Cell lines used for live - cell microscopy should be adherent cell cultures or be spun down on a support , such as glass coverslip . While the cell line to be used depends on the interest of the scientist , there are various considerations simplifying the data acquisition ( see Note 1 ) . 2 . Culture medium : use the standard medium required for the particular cell line . 3 . Prewarmed PBS containing 0 . 5 mM EDTA and 0 . 25 % trypsin in PBS . 4 . 0 . 2 % gelatin for coating the microscopy dishes or coverslips . Targeted Manipulation 203 5 . Plasmids : mammalian expression vectors coding for the setup of the targeting strategy of interest ( one carrying the GBP counterpart and one carrying the GFP ; see Notes 2 and 3 ) . Additional ﬂuorescent markers should be chosen according to the wavelengths that can be imaged using the microscope available . 6 . Transfection reagents : nucleofection system from Amaxa ( Lonza ) or Neon nucleofection system ( Thermo Fisher Scien - tiﬁc ) [ 16 ] , nucleofection solutions , cuvettes / tubes , and pip - ettes ( see Notes 4 and 5 ) . 7 . Microscopy dishes : form and size depends on the optical table inset available for the microscope . The bottom of the dish needs to be thin enough for higher magniﬁcation immersion lenses to be able to image through the sample . Material can be either glass or optical plastic ( see Note 6 ) . Glass lids are recom - mended for optimal contrast images . 8 . Microscope : for imaging of live cells and ﬁxed cells , we recom - mend the use of a spinning disc confocal microscope , charac - terized by high - speed acquisition and low level of phototoxicity to cells . The stage should be motorized to allow the acquisition of 3D stacks at several time points and several stage positions in one experiment . 3 Methods Here , we present a detailed protocol to target , manipulate or reposition speciﬁc factors and genomic regions to any desired loca - tion . The protocol is adapted to image ﬁxed cells on glass coverslips or to image living cells in a 35 mm diameter glass - bottomed dish : 1 . Prewarm growing medium and PBS – EDTA to 37 (cid:1) C and trypsin as well as transfection solutions to room temperature . 2 . Prepare the dish where transfected cells will be seeded by coating for 20 min with 0 . 2 % gelatin . Wash twice with pre - warmed medium to fully remove gelatin and add the ﬁnal volume of growing medium ( 2 mL for a 35 mm diameter dish ) and keep it in an incubator so that the medium reaches 37 (cid:1) C and CO 2 diffuses into it . 3 . Use 3 (cid:3) 10 5 adherently growing cells of a 10 cm diameter plate ( see Note 7 ) . Remove growing medium and wash carefully with 5 mL PBS – EDTA , avoiding detaching cells from the surface . Add 0 . 5 mL trypsin and incubate at 37 (cid:1) C for 2 – 5 min . Check cell detachment under a microscope . When most of the cells have detached from the substrate and are separated from each other , stop the enzymatic reaction by adding 4 . 5 mL growing medium . If cells are clumped together , carefully break up the 204 Kathrin S . Heinz and M . Cristina Cardoso cell clumps by pipetting up and down a couple of times . Cen - trifuge the cells for 6 min at 300 (cid:3) g . 4 . Prepare 100 μ L of transfection solution with the appropriate and optimized amount of plasmid DNA ( see Notes 8 and 9 ) . 5 . Once the cells are pelleted , discard the supernatant and care - fully resuspend in transfection solution . Transfer the cell sus - pension into an electroporation cuvette / tube . Make sure to avoid bubbles and that the solution is clear without phenol red , because this can cause error messages during the electropora - tion process . Immediately perform the electroporation using the appropriate program for your cells ( see Note 5 ) . Use the previously prepared dish from the incubator and seed cells into the dish . Carefully shake the plate to homogenously distribute the cell suspension and return it into the incubator . Incubate overnight ( see Notes 10 and 11 ) . 6 . On the next day , remove the medium and wash twice with prewarmed medium to remove dead cells , debris and add fresh medium . 7 . For ﬁxed cell studies , cells are ﬁxed with 4 % formaldehyde for 10 min , permeabilized for 20 min with 0 . 5 % Triton X - 100 – PBS prior to immunostainings with the desired anti - bodies ( see Note 12 ) . 8 . In case of live - cell imaging make sure that your incubation chamber is ready : 37 (cid:1) C , 5 % CO 2 and over 40 % humidity level . 9 . Place the dish with the transfected cells on the microscope . Allow the dish to acclimatize to new conditions prior to start - ing imaging . Slight changes in temperature may affect the material in such a way that the focal plane can change dramati - cally during the ﬁrst 10 – 20 min . 10 . Look for transfected cells by using short exposure times to minimize phototoxicity . Select cells that express the minimal amount of the ﬂuorescent proteins that can be imaged prop - erly . Too high expression levels may lower the chances that transfected cells will pass normally through S - phase and / or increases the chances that the cells undergo apoptosis . 11 . Set up the imaging conditions ﬁnding a compromise between phototoxicity and undersampling . The ideal conditions depend strongly on the cell line , since some cells are more sensitive to transfection and phototoxicity , as well as of course on the transfection strategy you have set up . In general , acquiring z - stacks at a time interval of 20 min is usually enough to follow changes of , for example , S - phase . The minimal amount to acquire an entire cell cycle depends on how fast the cells divide ( see Note 3 ) . Under normal conditions cells can be kept on the microscope stage and be imaged over 2 days . Targeted Manipulation 205 4 Notes 1 . Factors to consider when choosing a cell line to perform tar - geted manipulation and live - cell imaging of the targeting approach : – How well the cells can be transfected ( transfection and expression rate ) . – How the cells can tolerate imaging - derived phototoxicity . – How much the cells move , which makes long term imaging difﬁcult . – How fast cells divide and how they handle targeting in the subsequent cell cycles . 2 . Factors to consider when setting up your targeting approach : – Which factor is targeted ? – Where is the factor targeted ? – Are the target and / or the location speciﬁc enough for a manipulation ? 3 . We always suggest linking the GBP to the leading part of the targeting assay and the targeted factor to the GFP . With this setup you are directly able to check by eye whether your factor is targeted by visual inspection of the GFP signal . 4 . While a good transfection rate is a factor to consider when choosing your transfection method , when following cell cycle progression at a single cell level , it is more important to achieve a moderate expression level . We recommend the nucleofection system from Amaxa ( Lonza ) for somatic cells and Neon Nucleofection ( Thermo Fisher ) for embryonic stem cells , although other methods can be used . 5 . We suggest for myoblasts and ﬁbroblasts the B - 032 program ( e . g . , C2C12 , Microtus cabrerae ) and for mouse embryonic ﬁbroblasts the A - 024 program ( e . g . , MEF ) of the Amaxa machine . For mouse embryonic stem cells like J1 we suggest to use the Neon nucleofection system with a transfection setup of 1250 V , 20 ms width , and two pulses . 6 . Irrespective of whether you use your targeting approach for ﬁxed cell studies or live - cell imaging we highly suggest to coat glass surfaces with gelatin as this improved the fast attachment of transfected cells and increased the general transfection efﬁciency . 7 . Cell density is a key factor for live - cell imaging and to provide enough cells prior to transfection as a higher amount of cells is dying during the process of electroporation . While a too high density can result in cell contact inhibition , preventing cells from cycling , a too low density can result in cells moving 206 Kathrin S . Heinz and M . Cristina Cardoso more freely along growing surface , making it extremely hard to keep them in frame over several hours . In case of low transfec - tion efﬁciency the likelihood of having enough cells for your studies is further decreased . The optimal cell density depends on the cell line used : mouse myoblasts and ﬁbroblasts tend to move and a rather high density is recommended . In case of embryonic stem cells like for J1 for instance , a lower density makes more sense to avoid large colonies of cells , further complicate the imaging and validation of targeting in single cells . 8 . The optimal ratio of both plasmids is of upmost importance . Therefore we suggest ratio measurements before starting experiments . We always used combinations ( in μ g ) from 1 : 1 up to 3 : 3 , changing for every plasmid to make sure to achieve the perfect combination , resulting in healthy cells with typical morphology but an efﬁcient targeting with high transfection efﬁciency . 9 . Further optimization is needed when you want to combine your targeting approach with , for example , a PCNA transfec - tion to label active replication sites . We checked triple transfec - tions as well as quadruple transfections , both is suitable , but requires further optimization step . As already indicated , use as less plasmid as possible to not harm the cells too much but still enough to have an appropriate targeting efﬁciency . 10 . During optimization we recommend to check for the perfect incubation time after transfection . Too high expression levels may lower the chances that transfected will pass normally through S - phase and / or increases the chances that the cells undergo apoptosis . High targeted cells often appear fast after nucleofection but also die quite fast , so make sure to estimate the right level of targeting for your experiments . For imaging and reliable cell cycle studies , cells with low or mid expression rate are preferable . These cells appear slightly later after trans - fection process . 11 . During the establishment of different targeting strategies in different cell lines we always incubated in a range in between 20 and 24 h for ﬁrst cell cycle studies and up to 49 h for second cell cycle studies . But these numbers strongly depend on the cell line you are using and its doubling time . 12 . When targeted cells are used for ﬁxed cell studies like FISH , pulse labeling setups , or immunostainings in general , we sug - gest to boost the signal with an additional GBP ( 1 mg / mL ) incubation step prior to DAPI staining when the GFP signal is very weak . We suggest a step of 1 hour at room temperature . Targeted Manipulation 207 Acknowledgments We thank H . Cristina Cardoso Chapter 14 Visualization of Endogenous Transcription Factors in Single Cells Using an Antibody Electroporation - Based Imaging Approach Sascha Conic , Dominique Desplancq , Alexia Ferrand , Nacho Molina , Etienne Weiss , and La´szlo´ Tora Abstract In this chapter , we describe an antibody electroporation - based imaging approach that allows for precise imaging and quantiﬁcation of endogenous transcription factor ( i . e . , RNA Polymerase II ) distributions in single cells using 3D structured illumination microscopy ( 3D - SIM ) . The labeling is achieved by the efﬁcient and harmless delivery of ﬂuorescent dye - conjugated antibodies into living cells and the speciﬁc binding of these antibodies to the targeted factors . Our step - by - step protocol describes the procedure of the labeling of the speciﬁc antibodies , their electroporation into living cells , the sample preparation and 3D - SIM imaging as well as the postimaging analyses of the labeled endogenous transcription factors to obtain information about their nuclear distribution as well as their function . This protocol can be applied to a plethora of endogenous nuclear factors by using target speciﬁc noninhibiting antibodies . Key words Antibodies , Antibody delivery , Single cells , Endogenous proteins , RNA polymerase II , Transcription , Imaging , Nucleus , Factor distribution , 3D structured illumination microscopy ( 3D - SIM ) 1 Introduction Recent developments in high - resolution microscopy techniques [ 1 ] have revolutionized ﬂuorescence microscopy . Single - cell imaging has become a method of choice to visualize cellular components under physiological conditions and to decipher cellular processes . The detection of native proteins in their cellular context remains challenging , however . Imaging of proteins in live cells is widely achieved by exogenous overexpression of the proteins of interest fused to ﬂuorescent proteins ( FPs ) [ 2 – 4 ] . However , these fusions do not always behave like their unmodiﬁed counterparts [ 5 ] and do not always behave as native endogenous proteins . Moreover , post - translational modiﬁcations ( PTMs ) cannot directly be visualized Yaron Shav - Tal ( ed . ) , Imaging Gene Expression : Methods and Protocols , Methods in Molecular Biology , vol . 2038 , https : / / doi . org / 10 . 1007 / 978 - 1 - 4939 - 9674 - 2 _ 14 , © Springer Science + Business Media , LLC , part of Springer Nature 2019 209 with FPs . To overcome these limitations , mammalian expression constructs comprising the antigen - binding domains of nanobodies , chromobodies , or intrabodies were designed in fusion with green FP ( GFP ) to target endogenous proteins in living cells [ 6 – 8 ] . How - ever , these approaches are hampered by constitutive expression of the antibody probes that make it difﬁcult to discriminate between antigen - bound and unbound antibody - GFP signals [ 9 ] . Aggrega - tion of the antibody molecules in the reducing environment of the cytoplasm is a further limitation of the exogenous expression of certain recombinant antibodies [ 10 ] . For years , dye - conjugated antibodies have proven their efﬁ - ciency in immunoﬂuorescence experiments . As antibodies cannot efﬁciently penetrate through the cell membrane of living metazoan cells , to deliver antibodies in living cells methods such as microin - jection , osmotic lysis of pinocytic vesicles , loading with glass beads , pore - forming bacterial toxins , or protein transfection using various cationic lipids or polymers have been developed [ 11 – 13 ] . Such methods often require specialized know - how , are harmful to cells and / or suffer from low efﬁciency . We have developed an antibody - electroporation based imaging approach for conventional and high - resolution microscopy , which allows visualization of endogenous proteins in living cells using dye - conjugated antibodies or Fab fragments [ 14 ] . The labeled antibody probes are delivered into the cytoplasm of living cells by electroporation , with a cell viability of greater than 90 % [ 15 ] . Once in the cytoplasm , the labeled antibody ( 150 kDa ) binds to its endogenous target protein . For nuclear targets , the labeled antibody bound to its neosynthetized target is transported to the nucleus via a piggybacking mechanism . Dye - conjugated Fab fragments that are sufﬁciently small ( 50 kDa ) can be used to target nuclear proteins and to detect transient PTM in the nucleus because they can freely diffuse into the nucleus [ 14 , 16 ] . Interestingly , the percentage of antibody molecules deliv - ered into the cell is proportional to the antibody concentration in the electroporation mix , allowing for the delivery of desired num - ber of molecules of antibody probes in the cell . Thus , the desired number of endogenous targets can be visualized [ 17 ] . Further - more , the method is easy to carry out and can be used with many different dyes to perform multicolor imaging . Here we describe how to label , electroporate , image , and quantify an endogenous transcription factor in single cells using our method . As an example , we chose the visualization of the DNA - dependent RNA polymerase II transcription factor complex ( Pol II ) in human cell nuclei . Pol II has 12 subunits and RPB1 is its largest subunit that contains its C - terminal domain ( CTD ) that is composed of 52 CTD repeats in human cells . We describe our protocol to label anti - RPB1 monoclonal antibodies with ﬂuores - cent dyes ( Subheading 3 . 1 ) , deliver them into living cells by elec - troporation ( Subheading 3 . 2 ) , prepare the samples for 3D 210 Sascha Conic et al . structured illumination microscopy ( 3D - SIM ) ( Subheadings 3 . 3 and 3 . 4 ) and ﬁnally analyze the superresolution images to obtain information about endogenous RNA Pol II distribution ( Subhead - ing 3 . 5 ) . 2 Materials and Reagents 2 . 1 Antibody Labeling 1 . DeltaVision OMX SoftWoRx software . 2 . 5 Image Processing and Quantiﬁcation 1 . Fiji / Image J software . 2 . Imaris software . 3 . MATLAB software . 3 Methods All procedures in this protocol were performed at room tempera - ture if not mentioned otherwise . This protocol was optimized for human U2OS cells , but can be adapted to any adherent metazoan cell line . Use 500 μ L of buffer for every wash - step if 12 - well plates are used , otherwise the volume needs to be adjusted . In our experience , all ﬂuorophores from the Alexa Fluor and Atto families work very well for the labeling of antibodies . Other dyes and kits would need to be tested and optimized . The antibody used in this protocol for the labeling of the endogenous RNA Pol II was the anti - RPB1 7G5 [ 18 ] . Any other previously tested noninhibiting speciﬁc antibody can be used for the method , but needs to be tested before by immunoﬂuorescence for its binding properties to its target factor in cells [ 16 ] . The electroporation of antibodies is performed using the Neon transfection system and the corresponding Neon transduction kits . All buffers and solu - tions need to be ﬁltered and sterilized for electroporation to avoid contamination of the cells . Prewarm 2 . 5 % trypsin and the growth culture medium without antibiotics at 37 (cid:3) C prior to the electro - poration experiment . 212 Sascha Conic et al . 3 . 1 Fluorescent Labeling of Monoclonal Antibodies for the Imaging of Endogenous Factors 1 . Prepare 1 L of 0 . 1 M sodium bicarbonate pH 8 . 2 labeling buffer as described . Afterward , dialyze 100 μ g of antibody ( 7G5 mAb ) solution in a volume of 100 μ L ( 1 mg / mL ) against 1 L of 0 . 1 M sodium bicarbonate for 4 h at 4 (cid:3) C using DiaEasy dialyzing tubes ( see Note 1 ) . 2 . The labeling is performed using the Alexa Fluor 488 Monoclonal Antibody labeling kits from Invitrogen . Mix the anti - RPB1 anti - body solution with the Alexa 488 ﬂuorescent dyes as written in the manufacturer’s protocol and incubate at RT for 1 h in the dark . Mix the solution every 15 min by inverting the tube . Nonbound Alexa 488 dyes are removed by purifying the labeling mix using the gel ﬁltration columns supplied in the labeling kit ( see Note 2 ) . 3 . Concentrate the labeled anti - RPB1 antibody by using 0 . 5 mL Amicon ﬁlter units with a cutoff of 10 kDa . Centrifuge for 10 min at 14 , 000 (cid:1) g to concentrate the solution to a volume of approximately 50 μ L . Measure the concentration of the labeled antibody using a NanoDrop spectrophotometer and the Protein and Labels mode . 4 . Labeling efﬁciency can be calculated by measuring the absorp - tion at 280 and 494 nm ( Alexa 488 dye speciﬁc wavelength ) . The dye – antibody labeling ratio can then be calculated using the formula mentioned in the protocol of Invitrogen ( see Note 3 ) . 3 . 2 Electroporation of Fluorescently Labeled Antibodies Into U2OS Cells 1 . Prepare Eppendorf tubes containing 2 μ g of ﬂuorescently labeled anti - RPB1 antibodies ( one tube for each electropora - tion ) and keep them in the dark on ice ( see Note 4 ) . For example , transfer 2 μ L of anti - RPB1 – 488 antibody solution with a concentration of 1 mg / mL into each tube ( see Note 5 ) . 2 . Also prepare 12 well culture plates with high precision cover glasses ( see Note 6 ) and antibiotics free growth medium and store the plates in the incubator at 37 (cid:3) C to prewarm the medium ( see Note 7 ) . 3 . Trypsinize the cells by washing them ﬁrst twice with 5 mL of PBS and afterward by incubating them with 2 . 5 % trypsin for 4 min at 37 (cid:3) C . Dilute the detached cells in antibiotic - free growth medium . 4 . Count the cells and transfer a ﬁnal cell number of 8 (cid:1) 10 5 cells to a 15 - mL tube . Afterward , pellet the cells by centrifuging them at 200 (cid:1) g for 5 min . A total of eight transductions can be performed with this pellet as each electroporation uses 10 5 cells ( see Note 8 ) . 5 . Remove the growth medium and wash the cells with 4 mL of PBS . Pellet them again and resuspend the pellet in 80 μ L of resuspension buffer ( R - buffer ) ( see Note 9 ) . 6 . Mix 10 μ L of the resuspended cells with the antibody solution and pipet this mix with the Neon pipette using the 10 μ L Neon Visualization of Endogenous Factors Using Antibodies 213 tips . Air bubbles in the pipette tip should be avoided as they will induce an electric short - circuit which will kill the cells during the electroporation . 7 . After putting the Neon pipette into the pipette station , the electroporation is performed using the following parameters : Voltage : 1550 V . Number of pulses : 3 . Time width of pulse : 10 ms . 8 . Pipet the cells directly into the prewarmed medium of the 12 - well cell culture plate that was prepared in step 2 after the electric pulse and repeat the steps 6 and 7 until all transduction experiments have been performed . Afterward , incubate the cells at 37 (cid:3) C with 5 % CO 2 for 24 h ( see Notes 10 and 11 ) . 3 . 3 Sample Preparation for Superresolution Microscopy 1 . Prepare fresh 4 % PFA in PBS from a 16 % stock solution and prewarm it to 37 (cid:3) C in a water bath . 2 . 24 h after the electroporation , remove the growth medium and wash the cells once with PBS . Afterward , add 0 . 5 mL of pre - warmed 4 % PFA and incubate the cells for 5 min under shaking to ﬁx the cells . 3 . Wash the cells twice with PBS supplemented with 0 . 02 % Triton X - 100 and once with PBS for 5 min each ( see Note 12 ) . 4 . For DAPI staining , prepare a 1 / 2500 dilution of DAPI from a 1 mg / mL stock solution in dH 2 O and add it to the cells . Incubate the cells for 30 s under shaking before removing the DAPI solution and washing the cells with PBS . 5 . To mount the sample , take the coverslip and dip it in dH 2 O shortly , put the edge of the coverslip on a tissue paper to absorb the excess water by capillary forces . Mount the coverslip with 6 μ L of Vectashield mounting medium on a microscope slide and seal it with nail polish ( see Note 13 ) . Let the samples dry at room temperature for an hour , then store at 4 (cid:3) C in the dark . Examine the slides shortly after preparing them under the microscope ( same day or next day ) . 3 . 4 3D Structured Illumination Microscopy of Endogenous Transcription Factors 1 . Three - dimensional structured illumination microscopy ( 3D - SIM ) is performed on a DeltaVision OMX - Blaze V4 sys - tem equipped with a Plan Apo N (cid:1) 60 1 . 42 NA oil immersion objective lens ; four liquid - cooled sCMOS cameras ( pco . edge 5 . 5 , full frame 2560 (cid:1) 2160 ; PCO ) ; and 405 , 445 , 488 , 514 , 568 , and 642 nm solid - state lasers . 2 . Before imaging , use 0 . 5 μ m Tetraspeck beads to adjust the algorithm parameters . The images of a single bead acquired at different wavelength need to be overlapping . If this is not the 214 Sascha Conic et al . case , then the alignment parameters need to be adjusted which is usually done by the facility / lab owning the microscope . 3 . Use the 405 and 488 nm laser lines for DAPI and Alexa Fluor 488 detection respectively . Acquisition of endogenous RNA Pol II is performed with optical z - sections separated by 0 . 125 μ m and attenuated laser power of 10 or 31 . 3 % as well as exposure times between 75 and 400 ms ( see Note 14 ) . 4 . The raw images are processed and reconstructed using the DeltaVision OMX SoftWoRx software package ( v6 . 1 . 3 , Applied Precision , Issaquah , WA ) . Set the Wiener ﬁlter constant to 0 . 0050 for an optimal image reconstruction ( see Note 15 ) . 3 . 5 Image Analysis and Quantiﬁcation to Analyze Endogenous Transcription Factor Distribution 1 . The image processing to produce 3D images of the nucleus containing endogenous RNA Pol II is performed using the Imaris software ( Bitplane , Zurich , Switzerland ) ( see Fig . 1 ) . 2 . The Fiji / Image J software is used to count the RNA Pol II spots in the image and to obtain the 3D position as well as the volume of each spot . In particular , a Fiji / Image J Macro com - bining the 3D spot segmentation [ 19 ] as well as the 3D object counter [ 20 ] plugins is used for this quantiﬁcation . By using these plugins , the spots can be segmented by ﬁnding local maxima in the image and afterward a local Gaussian distribu - tion ﬁtting is performed . After obtaining the mask of each spot , factors like spot number or volume are computed . 3 . MATLAB ( MathWorks , Natick , MA ) is used to analyze the spot data and quantify the distribution of the number and volume of the spots corresponding to the endogenous tran - scription factor ( RNA Pol II ) molecules inside the nucleus and cytoplasm . DAPI images are used to determine whether a spot is inside or outside the nucleus . This is performed by smooth - ening and segmenting the DAPI images using a 3D Gaussian ﬁlter and the Minimum Cross Entropy thresholding algorithm ( see Fig . 2a , b ) [ 21 ] . Afterward , the distributions of spot volumes inside and outside the nucleus can be calculated ( see Fig . 2c and Note 16 ) . 4 Notes 1 . It is important to raise the pH of the antibody solution over a pH of 8 for the labeling reaction to increase labeling efﬁciency . It has been shown in our hands that a dialysis against the labeling buffer ( 0 . 1 M sodium bicarbonate ) results in better labeling efﬁciencies ( 3 – 4 dyes per molecule more ) than the pH raising step described in the protocol of Invitrogen . Visualization of Endogenous Factors Using Antibodies 215 2 . It is recommended to wash the gel ﬁltration column with PBS before loading the labeling reaction as any traces of NaN 3 that is present in the storage buffer of the gel ﬁltration beads will be removed . Fig . 1 Imaging of endogenous RNA Pol II in the nuclei of a human cell using 3D - SIM microscopy . U2OS cells were transduced with Alexa488 Fluor labeled anti - RPB1 antibodies and ﬁxed after 24 h . Afterward , the cells were analyzed using 3D - SIM microscopy . One representative 3D image of a nucleus is shown with antibody - labeled endogenous RNA Pol II spots . Scale bar : 2 μ m 216 Sascha Conic et al . 3 . The labeling kits from Invitrogen contain N - hydroxysuccinimide ester ﬂuorophores that react with the amine group at the tip of the side chain of lysines to label the antibodies . This works ﬁne with antibodies that do not harbor lysine residues in their binding site ( paratope ) . A more site - speciﬁc labeling strategy can be followed if the binding capacity of the labeled antibodies ( that can be easily tested by IF ) is affected by this technique . For this labeling procedure ( Fab’ ) 2 fragments need to be prepared , which can be speciﬁcally labeled at the typical cysteine residues in the C - terminal of the Fab’ ( hinge region ) with maleimide - activated ﬂuorophores upon mild reduction . This method preserves theoretically the antibody - binding site from any deleterious chemical alteration [ 22 ] . However , it only allows the addition of a maximum of two to three ﬂuorophore molecules per Fab’ fragment which is enough for confocal microscopy but too low for 3D - SIM microscopy . Fig . 2 Image analysis and quantiﬁcation of transcription factor clusters ( i . e . , RNA Pol II ) . ( a ) Smoothed and binarized projected image in the DAPI channel used to classify spots as inside or outside the nucleus . ( b ) Distribution of grey levels of the smoothed DAPI images . The red dot shows the threshold obtained with the Minimum Cross Entropy thresholding algorithm used in A to binarized the image . ( c ) Distribution of spot volumes of endogenous RNA Pol II in the cytoplasm ( blue ) and the nucleus ( red ) Visualization of Endogenous Factors Using Antibodies 217 4 . The puriﬁed antibodies need to be diluted in sterile PBS with no other ingredients prior to labeling and electroporation as preservatives like NaN 3 or traces of BSA will decrease the viability of your cells after electroporation signiﬁcantly . 5 . The working solution of labeled antibodies should have a concentration of 1 – 2 mg / mL . Higher concentration of the antibody solution decreases the volume needed for electropo - ration which should not exceed 5 μ L to avoid that the cells are getting too diluted . 6 . Make sure to use high quality cover glasses for the experiments with a precise thickness ( # 1 . 5 ) as they are important for the 3D - SIM imaging . It is also recommended to rinse them prior to use with 100 % acetone , distilled water and then 70 % ethanol . After washing , let them dry completely under the hood before use . 7 . If the cover glasses are transferred into the cell culture plate containing medium it is possible that air bubbles are formed under them which can lead to the settlement of cells under the cover glass instead of on it . Therefore , it is recommended to push them to the bottom of the well with the help of a pipette tip before adding the cells . 8 . In this protocol , 10 μ L Neon tips are used for the electropora - tion , but 100 μ L Neon tips can be used as well . However , the number of cells and labeled antibodies need to be adjusted accordingly . Every transduction uses 2 μ g of labeled anti - RPB1 antibodies and 10 5 cells . Therefore , with a pellet of 8 (cid:1) 10 5 cells , a total of eight electroporation experiments can be performed . However , even if a lower number of electropo - ration experiments are planned it is still recommended to keep a higher cell number as lower cell numbers will result in very small pellets and inaccuracies which can lower cell viability after electroporation drastically . 9 . After resuspending the cells in R - buffer , it is important to proceed quickly to the electroporation . If the cells remain longer than 15 min in R - buffer , it is possible that cell viability is decreasing signiﬁcantly . As the resuspension buffer ( R - buffer ) is part of the electroporation kit from Invitrogen , its composition is conﬁdential . However , we also tested 250 mM sucrose buffer in 1 (cid:1) PBS [ 23 ] or just simple 1 (cid:1) PBS which worked the same way as R - buffer for the electropo - ration of antibodies . 10 . The incubation time of the cells after electroporation of an anti - RPB1 antibody is approximately 24 h before the cells can be imaged under the microscope . This incubation time is speciﬁc for imaging RNA Pol II as the antibodies need to bind to the newly synthesized RPB1 protein in the cytoplasm 218 Sascha Conic et al . to get transported into the nucleus . Therefore , it depends on the neosynthesis rate of the nuclear target protein that is ana - lyzed using versatile antibody - based imaging approach ( VANIMA ) with labeled full - length antibodies . If other anti - bodies against other nuclear targets are used for VANIMA , this incubation time needs to be adjusted accordingly . However , it is also possible to use ﬂuorescently labeled Fab fragments , which are smaller than full length antibodies and can freely diffuse into the nucleus . This can lower the incubation time drastically and is especially important if the target protein has a very low neosynthesis rate or if PTMs in the nucleus want to be imaged [ 14 , 16 ] . 11 . It is also possible to perform live cell imaging of endogenous RNA Pol II using VANIMA . The labeling and electroporation steps are exactly the same for performing live cell imaging except that the cells should be transferred into a live imaging suitable cell culture dish after electroporation ( like 8 - well glass bottom μ - slides from ibidi ) . The sample preparation can be skipped afterward and the cells can be used directly for confocal live imaging of endogenous RNA Pol II [ 14 , 16 ] . 12 . It is possible that bright speckles can be detected during image acquisition outside of the cells on the cover glass . These speck - les correspond to nonelectroporated labeled antibodies , which stick to the cover glass surface . They are typically very bright and can induce artifacts during image reconstruction and therefore , if too many of these spots are detected it is recom - mended to increase the number of wash - steps from 3 to 6 after ﬁxation of the sample . It is also possible to include one more wash - step of 10 min with a buffer containing a higher concen - tration of Triton X - 100 ( 0 . 1 % Triton X - 100 in PBS ) to get rid of these speckles . 13 . It is recommended to use Vectashield H1000 or Prolong Dia - mond mounting medium for the experiments as they preserve the three - dimensional structure of the cells and are therefore highly suitable for 3D - SIM imaging . 14 . Test different refractive index oils to ﬁnd the best that match the sample . To get the best OMX - SIM reconstruction , it is recommended to image three channels maximum and the oil has to be chosen on the channel of most interest . Note that the choice of the oil is temperature dependent , so keep the tem - perature of the room constant during imaging . Select an expo - sure time that reduces photobleaching , while still achieving a signal to background ratio superior to 10 . Additionally , on the OMX Blaze microscope , select laser power and exposure time so that at least 2000 counts of intensity in the channel of interest are achieved . Visualization of Endogenous Factors Using Antibodies 219 15 . All reconstructed 3D - SIM images should be tested using the SIMCheck plugin for Fiji / Image J [ 24 ] . This plugin is a quality control for the acquired data and ensures that the detected and reconstructed data originates from real signal of the labeled antibodies and not from artifacts generated during image acquisition and reconstruction . 16 . Notice that the quantiﬁcation of the spot volume could be further used to estimate the number of endogenous transcrip - tion factor molecules in each spot by using the median volume of the cytoplasmic spots as a conversion factor . Like this , it would be possible to estimate how many transcription factor molecules are present in bigger clusters within the nucleus .
